тАШ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рджреЛрд░рднрдХреНрд╖рд┐’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рд╖рд╖реНрдардВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдХрд╛рдгреНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдЧрд╛рдерд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖реЗрдВ рд╕реЛрдорджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдореН ред рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдореА рдЬрдЧрддреА ред рд╕реЛрдореЛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХрд╛рдиреНрддрдВ- рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рджреЛрдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪреЛрдирд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЧрд╛рдердГ рд╕реМрдореНрдпрдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдВ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдореА рдЬрдЧрддреА’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд▓реИрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдХрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

48 (668)
Soma
Prag─Бtha Kaс╣Зva
15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 5
This well-known and frequently translated hymn is one of the very few dedicated to Soma outside of the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala, and as such does not concern тАЬself-purifyingтАЭ Soma (Soma Pavam─Бna), the subject of that maс╣Зс╕Нala. The preparation of soma is not treated here, save for a single reference (vs. 7) to it as тАЬpressed.тАЭ Instead the emphasis is on somaтАЩs effects, тАЬwhen drunkтАЭ (p─лt├б vss. 4, 5, 10, 12), on the drinker. The immediate effect is euphoria; as in the famous exultant boast in verse 3 тАЬwe have drunk the soma; we have become immortal; we have gone to the light; we have found the gods.тАЭ The soma produces a sense of space and boundlessness (vss. 1, 2, 5) while, paradoxically, being confined in the drinkerтАЩs body (vss. 2, 9, 10) and hold ing this body together (vs. 5). The temporal equivalent of this spatial expansion is the wish constantly expressed to тАЬlengthen our lifetimeтАЭ (vss. 4, 7, 10, 11). Soma is thus characterized by vitality, or life force, which he also confers on the drinker: the first and last verses of the hymn contain this signature word v├бyas.
The mood in the second half of the hymn darkens slightly. Though the poet still sees Soma as his protector and kindly comrade, he senses the threats that cause him to need that protectionтАФthreats from outside (vs. 8), from his own imperfect actions (vs. 9), and even from soma itself (vs. 10). Though he ultimately pronounces the threats vanquished (vs. 11), the mood of sheer exuberance has been broken.
The final few verses (12тАУ14) take a more ritual turn, with our ceremonial dedica tion of an oblation to soma, in his connection with the forefathers (who themselves receive soma, as is made clear elsewhere). The ancestor cult thus briefly surfaces here, and the emphasis throughout the hymn on lengthening our lifetimes (on earth) may provide a counterpoint to the ritually shaped afterlife inhabited by our ancestors.

English translation:

тАЬMay I, the wise and devout, enjoy the delicious, abundantly honoured Soma food, which all gods andmortals, pronouncing sweet, seek to obtain.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I of good wisdom have partaken of the vitality of the sweet drink, which is rich in purpose and excellent at finding wide space,
which all the gods and mortals, calling it honey, converge upon.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take sv─Бd├│с╕е as dependent on v├бyasaс╕е, not qualifying it (contra, e.g., GeldnerтАЩs тАЬvon dem s├╝ssen KrafttrunkтАЭ). Note that Soma is called vayodh─Б╠Бс╕е in the final vs. (15a) and is therefore not v├бyaс╕е himself.

s u v─Бdh├н yo opening p─Бda b echoes sv─Бd├│r opening a.

Griffith

WISELY have I enjoyed the savoury viand, religious-thoughted, best to find out treasure,
The food to which all Deities and mortals, calling it meath, gather themselves together.

Macdonell

I have partaken wisely of the sweet food That stirs good thoughts, best banisher of trouble, The food round which all deities and mortals, Calling it honey-mead, collect together,

Ich hab von dem s├╝├Яen Krafttrunk genossen, ich der Weise von dem Wohlmeinenden, der am besten einen Ausweg aus Not findet, den alle G├╢tter und Sterblichen Aufsuchen, ihn Honig nennend.

Ich nahm verst├дndig von der s├╝ssen Kost mir, die unter Andacht reichsten Segen spendet, An die die G├╢tter und die Menschen alle, sie Meth benennend, ins Gesammt heraugehn.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou enter within, and unimpaired, you avert the anger of the gods; Soma, enjoying the friendship ofIndra, may you bring us to wealth as a swift (horse) its burden.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

You enter within: the heart or the sacrificialchamber

Jamison Brereton

When you have gone within, you will become Aditi [/boundlessness], appeaser of divine wrath.
Drop, enjoying the comradeship of Indra, like an obedient mare
following the chariot-pole, you should follow riches to fulfillment.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda is a paradox, in that confinement within leads to boundlessness. Following Geldner et al., I take ca as a subordinator; the accentuation of pr─Б╠Бg─Б(с╕е) is ambiguous: the Pp. reads pr├б ag─Бс╕е, but pra-├бg─Бс╕е is equally possible (so Oldenberg).

How to resolve the sandhi in ┼Ыra├║с╣гс╣н─лva is discussed by Oldenberg at some length; with him I take it as a fem. nom. sg. ┼Ыra├║с╣гс╣н─л. The Pp. analyzes r─Бy├б as r─Бy├й, but r─Бy├бс╕е is also possible, either as gen. sg. or acc. pl. I take it as the latter. My tr. of this p─Бda is closest to RenouтАЩs.

Griffith

Tlou shalt be Aditi as thou hast entered within, appeaser of celestial anger.
Indu, enjoying Indra’s friendship, bring us - as a swift steed the car - forward to riches.

Macdonell

Thou shalt be Aditi when thou hast entered Within, appeaser of celestial anger. May’st thou, O drop, enjoying Indra’s friendship, Like willing mare the car, to wealth advance us.

Geldner

Wenn du ins Innere gegangen bist, sollst du zur Aditi werden, den g├╢ttlichen Zorn abwendend. O Saft, m├╢gest du dich der Freundschaft Indra┬┤s erfreuen und dich, um Reichtum zu gewinnen, wie eine folgsame Stute ins Joch schicken.

Grassmann

Du tratest ein bei mir, so sei mir heilvoll, und nimm hinweg von mir den Zorn der G├╢tter; O Indu, der du liebst des Indra Freundschaft, lenk her uns Reichthum, wie das Ross den Wagen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe drink the Soma, may we become immortal; we have attained the light of (heaven), we have knownthe gods; what now could the enemy do to us, or what, O immortal, should the aggriever do to the mortal?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 3.2.5: the past tense is used in the sense of wish, a┼Ыaс╣Гsadyotan─Бya bh┼лt─Бrthanirde┼Ыaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

We have drunk the soma; we have become immortal; we have gone to the light; we have found the gods.
What can hostility do to us now, and what the malice of a mortal, o immortal one?

Griffith

We have drunk Soma and become immortal; we have attained the light, the Gods discovered.
Now what may foeman’s malice do to harm us? What, O Immortal, mortal man’s deception?

Macdonell

We have drunk Soma and become immortal; We have attained the light the gods discovered. What can hostility now do against us? And what, immortal god, the spite of mortals?

Geldner

Wir haben jetzt Soma getrunken, Unsterbliche sind wir geworden; wir sind zum Lichte gelangt, wir haben die G├╢tter gefunden. Was kann uns jetzt die Mi├Яgunst antun, was die Hinterlist eines Sterblichen, o Unsterblicher?

Grassmann

Wir tranken Soma, wurden nun unsterblich, erlangten Glanz und fanden auf die G├╢tter; Was kann uns schaden nun der B├╢sen Rotte? unsterblicher, des Sterblichen Gewaltthat?

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬO soma, drunk by us, be bliss to our hearts, as a father is indulgent to a son or a friend to a friend; OSoma, worthy of wide praise, do you, wise one, extend our years that we may live.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Become weal for our heart when drunk, o drop, very kindly, like a father to a son,
like a comrade to a comrade, you who are widely proclaimed as
insightful. Lengthen our lifetime, for us to live, Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the faint echo p─лt├б тАж pit├й(va).

Griffith

Absorbed into the heart, be sweet, O Indu, as a kind father to his son, O Soma,
As a wise Friend to friend: do thou, wide-ruler, O Soma, lengthen out our days for living.

Macdonell

Be cheering to our heart when drunk, O Indu, Kindly, like father to his son, O Soma. Like friend for friend, far-famed one, wisely Prolong our years that we may live, O Soma.

Geldner

Bekomm unserem Herzen wohl, wenn du getrunken bist, o Somasaft, freundlich wie ein Vater zu seinem Sohn, wie ein Freund dem Freunde, du der Weise, dessen Wort weithin gilt. Verl├дngere unser Lebensalter zum Leben, Soma!

Grassmann

Sei unserm Herzen hold, getrunkner Indu, uns liebreich Soma, wie dem Sohn der Vater, Wie Freund dem Freunde treu, der weit du herrschest, verl├дngre, Soma, unsres Lebens Dauer.

Elizarenkova

рдЗрдореЗ рдкреАрддрд╛рдГ рдпрд╢рд╕рдГ рдпрд╢рд╕реНрдХрд░рд╛рдГ рдЙрд░реБрд╖реНрдпрд╡рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдГ рд╕реЛрдорд╛рдГ рдЧрд╛рд╡рдГ рдЧреЛрд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рд░рднреВрддрд╛ рд╡рдзреНрд░реНрдпрдГ рд░рдердВ рди рд░рдердорд┐рд╡ рддрд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рд░рдердВ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд░рд╕реНрддрдВ рдкрд░реНрд╡рд╕реБ рд╕рдордирд╛рд╣ рд╕рдВрджрдзрддреЗ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдорд╛рдВ рдкреАрддрд╛рдГ рд╕реЛрдорд╛рдГ рдкрд░реНрд╡рд╕реБ рд╕рдВрдирд╣реНрдпрдиреНрддреБ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рддреЗ рд╕реЛрдорд╛рдГ рдорд╛ рдорд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд░рд╕рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреН рдЪрд░рд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рддреН рдЪрд░рдгрд╛рджрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдирд╛рддреН рд░рдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддреБ ред рд╕реЛрдордГ рдкреАрддрд╢реНрдЪреЗрддреН рдХрд░реНрдо рд╣реНрдпрд╡рд┐рд╕реНрд░рд╕реНрддрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдорд╛ рдорд╛рдВ рд╕реНрд░рд╛рдорд╛рддреН рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдзреЗрдГ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН рдЗрдиреНрджрд╡рдГ рдкреАрддрд╛рдГ рдпрд╡рдпрдиреНрддреБ рдкреГрдердХреНрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреБ рее рее резрез рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay these glory-conferring protecting Soma-streams knit together my joints as cows draw together achariot falling in pieces; may they keep us from a loosely-knit worship; may they deliver me from sickness.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Cows:g─Бvaс╕е = Soma streams, as the Soma is mixed with milk, and thus considered the product of the cows; aloosely-knit worship: when the Soma is drunk, the ceremony becomes consolidated

Jamison Brereton

These glorious (drops), when drunk, seek wide space. As cows [=leather straps] do a chariot, it [=soma] knots (me) together in my joints.
Let the drops guard me from my foot slipping, and let them keep me away from lameness.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On an─Бha see K├╝mmelтАЩs length and useful disc. (289). Flg. Oldenberg (accepted by K├╝mmel), I take it as a 3rd sg., not 2nd pl. with Geldner, Renou The nom. pl. im├й тАж p─лt─Б╠Бya┼Ы├бsa uruс╣гy├бvaс╕е of p─Бda a is (silently) resumed by sg. тАЬsoma.тАЭ In order to demonstrate the change in number of the subject, my tr. appears to treat p─Бda a as a separate clause, which of course it is not. Among other things, the m─Б in WackernagelтАЩs Position in a is the obj. of s├бm an─Бha in b.

Like 2a this hemistich is a paradox: the soma drops тАЬseeking wide spaceтАЭ nonetheless tie the drinker together.

Griffith

These glorious drops that give me freedom have I drunk. Closely they knit my joints as straps secure a car.
Let them protect my foot from slipping on the way: yea, let the drops I drink preserve me from disease.

Macdonell

These glorious, freedom-giving drops, when drunk by me, Have knit my joints together as do thongs a car. May these protect me now from fracturing a limb. And may they ever keep me from disease remote.

Geldner

Getrunken werden diese geehrten Somatr├дnke meine Nothelfer. Wie die Riemen den Wagen haltet ihr mich in den Gedanken zusammen. Diese S├дfte sollen mich vor Beinbruch beh├╝ten und mich vor L├дhmung bewahren.

Grassmann

Ihr Tr├дnke hehr und h├╝lfreich habt befestigt mich an den Gelenken, wie den Wagen Riemenwerk, Sie m├╢gen sch├╝tzen vor dem Gleiten meinen Fuss, und sie, die Indu’s, vor Verrenkung wahren mich.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSoma, kindle me like the fire ignited by attrition, brighten (our eyes) and make us rich; I praise you nowfor exhilaration; come now, full of wealth, to nourish us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You have enflamed me like a churned fire. Make us conspicuous; make us better off,
for now in the exhilaration of you, Soma, I think of myself as a rich man. I shall advance to prosperity.

Jamison Brereton Notes

did─лpaс╕е must be a redupl. aor. corresponding to trans.-caus. d─лp├бyati, despite the light redupl. We expect *d─лd─лpaс╕е or even *d─лdipaс╕е (which is found in B.E.

acdg. to WhitneyтАЩs Rts).

P─Бda-final naс╕е serves as object to both verbs in b.

All standard treatments take pr├б car─Б as 2nd sg. impv., but I think it works better as 1st sg. subjunctive. See also IX.82.4.

Griffith

Make me shine bright like fire produced by friction: give us a clearer sight and make us better.
For in carouse I think of thee, O Soma, Shall I, as a rich man, attain to comfort?

Macdonell

Like fire produced by friction, make me brilliant; Do thou illumine us and make us richer; For then I seem in thy carouse, O Soma, Enriched. Now enter us for real welfare.

Geldner

Wie das ausgeriebene Feuer sollst du mich entflammen. Erleuchte, mach uns besser! Denn nun in deinem Rausche, o Soma, komme ich mir wie ein Reicher vor. Schreite vorw├дrts zum Gedeihen!

Grassmann

O mache hell mich wie entflammtes Feuer, erleuchte uns und mach an Gut uns reicher; In deinem Rausch, o Soma, sprech’ zu mir ich: ┬╗Ein reicher Mann gelang’ ich jetzt zur Wohlfahrt.┬л

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMay we partake of you, effused, with a longing mind as (men enjoy) paternal wealth; King Soma,prolong our lives, as the sun the world-establishing day.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With a vigorous mind we would take a share of you when pressed, as of ancestral wealth.
King Soma, lengthen our lifetimes, like the sun the dawning days.

Griffith

May we enjoy with an enlivened spirit the juice thou givest, like ancestral riches.
O Soma, King, prolong thou our existence as Surya makes the shining days grow longer.

Macdonell

Of this thy juice pressed out with mind devoted, We would partake as of paternal riches. Prolong the years of life for us, King Soma, As S┼лrya lengthens out the days of spring-time.

Potency and battle fervor are on the rise, o drop. DonтАЩt hand us over (to the battle fervor) of the stranger, at his wish.

Spirit and power are fresh in us, O Indu give us not up unto our foeman’s pleasure.

English translation:

тАЬO Soma, you are the guardian of our bodies, you dwell in each limb as the beholder of man; though weimpair your rites, yet, divine one, bless us, you who are possessed of most excellent food and good friends.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For as protector of our body, Soma, you have settled down in every limb, having your eyes on men.
If we will confound your commandments, be merciful to us, as our
good comrade, all the more, o god.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Because of its accent niс╣гas├бtth─Б(с╕е) must still be under the domain of h├н in p─Бda a, contra Geldner, who takes a as a nominal clause and b as independent.

Griffith

For thou hast settled in each joint, O Soma, aim of men’s eyes and guardian of our bodies.
When we offend against thine holy statutes, as a kind Friend, God, best of all, be gracious.

Macdonell

Thou, as the guardian of our body, Soma, Surveying men, in every limb hast settled. If we perchance infringed, O god, thy statutes, As our good friend for greater wealth be gracious.

Geldner

Denn du bist der H├╝ter unseres Leibes, Soma; in jedem Gliede hast du Platz genommen als Aufseher. Wenn wir die Gel├╝bde brechen, so verzeih uns als guter Freund, o Gott, zu unserem Besten!

Grassmann

Denn du bist, Soma, unsres Leibes H├╝ter, in jedes Glied hast du gesetzt dich wachsam; Wenn deine Satzung je wir ├╝bertreten, o Gott, verzeih uns, sei uns hold und freundlich.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMay I obtain a wholesome friend who, when quaffed, will not harm me, O lord of bay horses; I ask ofIndra a long permanence for this Soma which has been plural ced within us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Might I be accompanied by a tender-hearted comrade, who would not harm me when it has been drunk, o possessor of fallow bay horses.
This soma here that has been deposited in usтАФfor it I go to Indra to lengthen our lifetime.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. harya┼Ыva (always elsewhere of Indra) is presumably addressed to a previously absent Indra, who surfaces by name in d – though it could also be referring to soma’s color.

Griffith

May I be with the Friend whose heart is tender, who, Lord of Bays! when quaffed will never harm me-
This Soma now deposited within me. For this, I pray for longer life to Indra.

Macdonell

I would accompany the friend, the wholesome. Who, Lord of Bays, imbibed, would never hurt me. I come to Indra to prolong our life-time, That we may relish Soma placed within us.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay those irremovable sicknesses depart; let those strong (pains) which have made us tremble, beafraid; the mighty Soma has climbed into us, we have attained that (draught) by which men prolong life.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These famines and diseases have gone off. Those allied to darkness have shied away; they have become afraid.
Soma has mounted us to his full extent. We have gone to where they lengthen lifetime.

Jamison Brereton Notes

├бnir─Б- is lit. тАШwant of nourishmentтАЩ. Since ├нr─Б- sometimes seems specialized for liquid nourishment, I considered тАШthirstsтАЩ here, and indeed in VIII.60.20, conjoined with kс╣г├║dham тАШhungerтАЩ, тАШthirstтАЩ works well. But in this passage such a translation sounds as if it refers to desires or cravings, and I think the passage refers to external threats rather than those generated within the person.

Griffith

Our maladies have lost their strength and vanished: they feared, and passed away into the darkness.
Soma hath risen in us, exceeding mighty, and we are come where men prolong existence.
12, Fathers, that Indu which our hearts have drunken, Immortal in himself, hath entered mortals.
So let us serve this Soma with oblation, and rest securely in his grace and favour.

Macdonell

Away have fled those ailments and diseases; The powers of darkness have been all affrighted. With mighty strength in us has Soma mounted: We have arrived where men prolong existence.

Geldner

Verschwunden sind jetzt Verschmachtung und Krankheiten; die finsteren M├дchte sind verscheucht, sie haben Furcht bekommen. Der Soma ist in uns aufgestiegen, seine Lebenskr├дfte entfaltend. Wir sind da angelangt, wo man das Leben verl├дngert.

Grassmann

Geschwunden sind nun Krankheit und Entkr├дftung, zerstoben und entflohn vor Angst die Dr├дnger; Schon hat der starke Soma uns bestiegen, jetzt sind wir da, wo lang das Leben dauert.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSoma, you in conjunction with the fathers do stretch our successively heaven and earth– to you let usdo worship with oblations, may we be lords of wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, coming to agreement with the forefathers, extend through heaven and earth.
To you, drop, we would do ceremonial honor with an oblation. May we be lords of riches.

Griffith

Associate with the Fathers thou, O Soma, hast spread thyself abroad through earth and heaven.
So with oblation let us serve thee, Indu, and so let us become the lords of riches,

Macdonell

Uniting with the Fathers thou, O Soma, Hast over Heaven and Earth thyself extended. So, Indu, we would serve thee with oblation: Thus we would be the lords of ample riches.

Geldner

Du, Soma, bist mit den V├дtern im Einvernehmen, du reichst so weit wie Himmel und Erde. Dir, o Saft, wollen wir darum mit Opfer aufwarten; wir wollen Herren der Reicht├╝mer sein.

Grassmann

O Soma, du vereinigt mit den V├дtern, hast dich verbreitet ├╝ber Erd’ und Himmel; Dem Indu m├╢chten wir mit Opfer dienen, und m├╢chten sein Besitzer aller Sch├дtze.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGuardian gods, speak favourably to us; let no dreams nor the censurer overpower us; may we be everdear to Soma; possessed of brave offspring, may we utter our hymn.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Protector Gods, speak on our behalf. Let sleep not master us, nor mumbling.
May we, always dear to Soma, possessed of good heroes, announce the ceremonial honor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On ─л┼Ыata see comm. ad I.23.9.

V─Бlakhilya

Griffith

Give us your blessing, O ye Gods’ preservers. Never may sleep or idle talk control us.
But evermore may we, as friends of Soma, speak to the synod with brave sons around us.

Macdonell

Do ye, protecting gods, speak in our favour, Let neither sleep nor idle talk subdue us; May we, for evermore, beloved of Soma, Endowed with hero sons, address the synod.

Ihr sch├╝tzenden G├╢tter verteidigt uns! Nicht soll uns der Schlaf ├╝bermannen, noch sinnlose Rede. Wir wollen allezeit dem Soma lieb sein und als Meister Worte der Weisheit reden.

Grassmann

H├╝lfreiche G├╢tter, sprecht uns freundlich Muth ein, nicht Schlaf bezwing’ uns, nicht geheimes Fl├╝stern, Geliebt von Soma m├╢gen ├╝berall wir, Umschart von M├дnnern, die Versammlung leiten.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, give us food from every side; you are the bestower of heaven; enter us, beholder of men; OSoma, rejoicing with your protecting powers, guard us from behind and before.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With your protecting powers:┼лtyaс╕е = Maruts, gant─Бraс╕е, ava gatau

Jamison Brereton

You, o Soma, confer vitality on us on all sides; you, as finder of the sun, possessing the eye of menтАФenter us.
You, o drop, along with your helpтАФprotect us from behind and also from in front.
Va╠Дlakhilya Hymns
The following eleven hymns (VIII.49тАУ59) are known as the V─Бlakhilya hymns. These are apocryphal or, in GeldnerтАЩs felicitous description, тАЬhalf-apocryphalтАЭ (halbapokryph). A number of khil─Бni or apocrypha were transmitted in the R╠еgvedic tradition, but only these eleven (or, in some other reported recensions, somewhat fewer) were inserted into and transmitted within the R╠еgveda Saс╣Гhit─Б
itself, as well as in the khil─Бni collections. Moreover, these eleven were trans mitted with accents and were treated in the Padap─Бс╣нha, the Anukramaс╣З─л (save for the tenth, VIII.58), and so forth, though they were not commented on by S─Бyaс╣Зa in his R╠еgvedic commentary. In our R╠еgveda recension, the ┼Ъ─Бkalya, they were inserted between the sixth and seventh anuv─Бkas of VIII, though they are reported to appear elsewhere in other recensions, not always in a single group. The Grassmann numbers, 1018тАУ1028, reflect the status of these hymns as addi tions to the original saс╣Гhit─Б.
The text of these hymns is in general less well transmitted than the rest of the R╠еgveda, and the hymns themselves sometimes have the air of a school exer cise. Notable in this connection is the fact that the first eight hymns proceed in pairs, each pair dedicated to the same divinity (except for a few verses in the third pair, VIII.53тАУ54) and containing the same number of verses in the same meter (except for a few verses in the last pair, VIII.55тАУ56). Moreover, the first pair (VIII.49тАУ50) and, to a much lesser extent, the second pair (VIII.51тАУ52) follow the same model, verse by verse, often using identical or near identical vocabulary but varying grammar, or else employing transparent lexical sub
stitution but keeping the grammar the same, and one can imagine that the two hymns represent separate realizations of a set pedagogical task. However, whatever the reason for their coupling, the pairs afford us interesting insights into the composition of R╠еgvedic hymns. For this reason, as well as the fact that puzzles in one hymn of the pair are sometimes illuminated by the parallel passages in the other, we will comment on the first two sets of paired hymns together.

Griffith

On all sides,. Soma, thou art our life-giver: aim of all eyes, light-finder, come within us.
Indu, of one accord with thy protections both from behind and from before preserve us.

Macdonell

Thou, Soma, givest strength to us on all sides. Light-finder, watching men, within us enter. Do thou, O Indu, with thine aids accordant, Behind for ever and before protect us.

Geldner

Sei du, o Soma, uns allenthalben ein Kraftverleiher, geh als Himmelslichtfinder, als Aufseher in uns ein! Sch├╝tze du Saft uns im Verein mit deinen Schutzgeistern von hinten oder auch von vorn!

Grassmann

In uns geh ein von allen Seiten, Soma, uns Glanz verschaffend, auf uns M├дnner schauend, O Indu, du vereint mit deinen H├╝lfen, beschirme uns von vorne und von hinten.

Elizarenkova
